[user] <command-message>loop</command-message>
<command-name>/loop</command-name>
<command-args>5m /biff:read</command-args>

[user] # /loop — schedule a recurring prompt

Parse the input below into `[interval] <prompt…>` and schedule it with CronCreate.

## Parsing (in priority order)

1. **Leading token**: if the first whitespace-delimited token matches `^\d+[smhd]$` (e.g. `5m`, `2h`), that's the interval; the rest is the prompt.
2. **Trailing "every" clause**: otherwise, if the input ends with `every <N><unit>` or `every <N> <unit-word>` (e.g. `every 20m`, `every 5 minutes`, `every 2 hours`), extract that as the interval and strip it from the prompt. Only match when what follows "every" is a time expression — `check every PR` has no interval.
3. **Default**: otherwise, interval is `10m` and the entire input is the prompt.

If the resulting prompt is empty, show usage `/loop [interval] <prompt>` and stop — do not call CronCreate.

Examples:
- `5m /babysit-prs` → interval `5m`, prompt `/babysit-prs` (rule 1)
- `check the deploy every 20m` → interval `20m`, prompt `check the deploy` (rule 2)
- `run tests every 5 minutes` → interval `5m`, prompt `run tests` (rule 2)
- `check the deploy` → interval `10m`, prompt `check the deploy` (rule 3)
- `check every PR` → interval `10m`, prompt `check every PR` (rule 3 — "every" not followed by time)
- `5m` → empty prompt → show usage

## Interval → cron

Supported suffixes: `s` (seconds, rounded up to nearest minute, min 1), `m` (minutes), `h` (hours), `d` (days). Convert:

| Interval pattern      | Cron expression     | Notes                                    |
|-----------------------|---------------------|------------------------------------------|
| `Nm` where N ≤ 59   | `*/N * * * *`     | every N minutes                          |
| `Nm` where N ≥ 60   | `0 */H * * *`     | round to hours (H = N/60, must divide 24)|
| `Nh` where N ≤ 23   | `0 */N * * *`     | every N hours                            |
| `Nd`                | `0 0 */N * *`     | every N days at midnight local           |
| `Ns`                | treat as `ceil(N/60)m` | cron minimum granularity is 1 minute  |

**If the interval doesn't cleanly divide its unit** (e.g. `7m` → `*/7 * * * *` gives uneven gaps at :56→:00; `90m` → 1.5h which cron can't express), pick the nearest clean interval and tell the user what you rounded to before scheduling.

## Action

1. Call CronCreate with:
   - `cron`: the expression from the table above
   - `prompt`: the parsed prompt from above, verbatim (slash commands are passed through unchanged)
   - `recurring`: `true`
2. Briefly confirm: what's scheduled, the cron expression, the human-readable cadence, that recurring tasks auto-expire after 7 days, and that they can cancel sooner with CronDelete (include the job ID).
3. **Then immediately execute the parsed prompt now** — don't wait for the first cron fire. If it's a slash command, invoke it via the Skill tool; otherwise act on it directly.

## Input

   claude:tty25  Sun Jul 05 02:47  Bug report from vox (COO) — the agent-def    
                                   make-check hook you generate hides failures.
                                   Source: internal/hook/generate_agents.go
                                   (~L362), the PostToolUse: Write|Edit command
                                   it emits. SYMPTOM: after an agent edits a
                                   code file, the hook runs `make check`; on
                                   failure the agent/user see only
                                   "PostToolUse:Edit hook returned blocking
                                   error … No stderr output" — with NO reason.
                                   The actual make check failure is invisible.
                                   ROOT CAUSE: the hook pipes make check output
                                   to STDOUT (`printf '%s\n' "$_out" | head -n
                                   60;
   claude:tty25  Sun Jul 05 02:47  exit $_rc`), but Claude Code's block         
                                   notification surfaces STDERR (empty here). So
                                   the failure detail is swallowed, and a
                                   non-`2` exit code isn't reliably fed back to
                                   the model. FIX (all 3 occurrences of the run-
                                   make-check branch in that Fprintf string):
                                   change … | head -n 60; exit $_rc to if [ $_rc
                                   -ne 0 ]; then … | head -n 60 >&2; exit 2; fi;
                                   exit 0 i.e. on FAILURE route output to stderr
                                   and exit 2 (so Claude Code shows it AND hands
                                   it to the agent to fix); on SUCCESS be silent
                                   (also drops the
   claude:tty25  Sun Jul 05 02:47  success-case noise). generate_agents_test.go 
                                   will need its expected-string updated. KEEP
                                   the per-edit coverage — do NOT move it to a
                                   Stop hook or lighten frequency. Jim is
                                   explicit: catching breakage immediately per-
                                   edit (not letting it accumulate to surface
                                   later) is the whole point. This change only
                                   makes the failure visible/actionable; same
                                   immediacy. Separately worth flagging to Jim
                                   on your side: the per-edit FULL `make check`
                                   (~70s) after every edit makes specialist
                                   agents slow and token-heavy — but
   claude:tty25  Sun Jul 05 02:47  that's his deliberate tradeoff, so it stays  
                                   unless he says otherwise. This report is only
                                   about fixing the invisible-failure bug. Want
                                   me to open a vox-side issue reference or is
                                   an ethos bead enough? — claude:tty25 (vox
                                   COO)

This is a real bug report from vox's COO. Let me verify it against the actual source before acting.

[assistant] Bug verified. Line 362 in `generate_agents.go` emits the hook command with 3 identical `make check` branches, each doing `... | head -n 60; exit $_rc`. On failure that sends detail to **stdout** and exits with make's raw code — but Claude Code only surfaces **stderr** for a blocking hook, and only **exit 2** reliably feeds the reason back to the model. So the failure detail is swallowed exactly as reported. The proposed fix (route to stderr + `exit 2` on failure, silent `exit 0` on success) is correct.

This is ethos-owned code, so an ethos bead is sufficient — no vox-side issue needed. Let me reply to vox COO.

## Result

**Before/after tail (per branch, as executed shell):**
- Before: `printf '%s\n' "$_out" | head -n 60; exit $_rc`
- After: `if [ $_rc -ne 0 ]; then printf '%s\n' "$_out" | head -n 60 &gt;&amp;2; exit 2; fi; exit 0`

**All 3 branches changed** — no-jq, empty-path, extension-match. `replace_all` reported "All occurrences were successfully replaced," and the emitted `command:` line at `internal/hook/generate_agents.go:362` shows the new tail in all three positions.

**make check:** passes.
`all checks passed (30 identities, 3 teams, 198 attributes)` — every package `ok`, markdownlint `0 error(s)`. Ran clean after both the impl commit and the CHANGELOG commit.

**Commits:**
- `bea460e` fix(hook): surface make-check failures on stderr, exit 2 (ethos-bo84) — `generate_agents.go` + `generate_agents_test.go`
- `5c2682e` docs(changelog): note make-check hook stderr/exit-2 fix (ethos-bo84)

**Emitted command verified.** The full-string test assertions in `generate_agents_test.go` (lines 210/391/420/730) were updated byte-for-byte and pass, so generation emits exactly the intended command. I reconstructed that emitted command into `/Users/jfreeman/Coding/punt-labs/ethos/.tmp/emitted.sh` and confirmed:
- `sh -n` → SYNTAX OK (POSIX-sh / dash clean; no bashisms)
- failure case (`_rc=1`) → exit 2, output on stderr, stdout empty
- success case (`_rc=0`) → exit 0, both streams silent

**Escaping note (no ambiguity, resolved):** the Go literal uses `%%s` (Fprintf → `%s`), `\\\\n` (→ YAML `\\n` → shell `\n`), and `\\\"` (→ YAML `\"` → shell `"`). The new `&gt;&amp;2`, `exit 2`, and `exit 0` tokens contain no `%`, quote, or backslash, so they needed no additional escaping — they pass through Fprintf and YAML unchanged.

**Test semantics updated:** the former "propagates make check exit code" case asserted `exit $_rc`, which no longer appears. It's now "PostToolUse surfaces make check failures on stderr" and asserts `_rc=$?`, `head -n 60 &gt;&amp;2`, and `exit 2`, while keeping the `make check) 2&gt;&amp;1 | head` regression guard.

**In-scope comment fixes:** updated the two stale doc comments in `generate_agents.go` (the branch-3 description and the trailing rationale) to state the exit-2/stderr behavior and cite ethos-bo84, since they described the old exit-code-propagation semantics.

One live observation: the PostToolUse hook that fired on my own edits during this task is the currently-installed (old) agent definition — it blocked twice with exactly the "No stderr output" symptom this change fixes. That is the bug reproduced firsthand; the fix will take effect once agent files are regenerated and reinstalled.

<note>A task-notification fires each time this agent stops with no live background children of its own. The user can send it another message and resume it, so the same task-id may notify more than once.</note>
<result>I have enough to assess. No test executes the generated PostToolUse command as a shell script; all coverage is string comparison on the generated YAML.

## Summary

The updated tests pin the new text correctly but not the new behavior. Four exact-string `want` blocks (lines 210, 391, 420, 730) were regenerated to include the full new command across all three make-check branches, and one dedicated test (renamed, lines 736-768) adds targeted substring assertions. This is solid regression protection against textual drift, but every assertion is a string comparison on generated YAML — nothing executes the emitted `/bin/sh` command, so no test proves the contract the PR exists to deliver (stderr + exit 2 on failure, silent + exit 0 on success).

## Answers to the four questions

**(1) Do the assertions pin the new behavior, or just match a string?** They pin the string, not the behavior. The four exact-match blocks reproduce the entire command verbatim including `head -n 60 &gt;&amp;2; exit 2; fi; exit 0` in every branch. That is the strongest possible textual pin — a single-branch revert fails the exact match. But it is purely lexical: if the command were regenerated with a logic inversion (`-eq 0` instead of `-ne 0`) or a mis-nested `if/fi`, and the expected strings were hand-updated to match, these tests would pass on a broken command. The assertions verify "the generator emits this text," not "this text does the right thing."

**(2) Are all three branches covered?** Yes, at the string level. The four exact blocks contain the new `&gt;&amp;2; exit 2; fi; exit 0` pattern in all three branches: no-jq (`if ! command -v jq`), empty-path (`if [ -z "$_path" ]`), and extension-match (`*.go|...) ... ;;`). A revert of any one branch breaks the exact-string tests.

**(3) Missing "failure is NOT silent" / "success IS silent" cases?** Yes — both are absent as behavioral assertions.
- No test drives the command with a failing `make check` and observes stderr non-empty + exit code 2.
- No test drives it with a passing `make check` and observes stdout/stderr empty + exit code 0. The dedicated test (lines 742-768) has zero success-path assertions; `exit 0` correctness is only positional inside the exact-string blocks.
- `internal/hook/subprocess_test.go` already has a `/bin/sh -c` execution harness (lines 411-443, used for a stdin-accessibility concern), so the infrastructure to run an emitted hook command under a shell exists in this package. A behavioral test is low-cost here.

**(4) Boundary/regression cases to add.** The dedicated test's substring assertions are individually weak: `assert.Contains(content, "exit 2")` and `assert.Contains(content, "head -n 60 &gt;&amp;2")` each pass on a single occurrence, so that test *in isolation* would not catch a one-branch revert (the other two branches still contain the tokens). It relies entirely on the exact-string blocks for per-branch coverage. There is also no negative assertion that the old `exit $_rc` form is gone — a partial revert to `head -n 60; exit $_rc` in one branch is caught only by the exact blocks, not by the behavioral test that is supposed to own this contract.

## High-confidence gaps

**Gap 1 — no execution test for the emitted command (criticality 7).** `internal/hook/generate_agents_test.go:742-768`. The test named "PostToolUse surfaces make check failures on stderr" asserts on generated text, never on generated behavior. Add a test that writes the emitted command to a script (or `sh -c`) with a stub `make` on PATH: (a) stub exits non-zero → assert process exit code == 2 and stderr contains the truncated output and stdout is empty; (b) stub exits 0 → assert exit code == 0 and both streams empty. This is the only way to catch a logic inversion, broken `if/fi` nesting, or a dash-incompatibility regression — exactly the failure class the PR comment claims to guard (ethos-bo84, POSIX-sh/dash compatibility). String tests cannot catch these because the expected strings are hand-maintained alongside the generator.

**Gap 2 — success path (silent + exit 0) has no dedicated assertion (criticality 4).** `internal/hook/generate_agents_test.go:750-759`. The dedicated behavioral test asserts only the failure tokens. Half the new contract ("on success it is silent and exits 0") is verified only positionally in the exact-string blocks. Fold a success-path check into Gap 1's execution test, or at minimum add a comment-anchored assertion that each branch ends `...; fi; exit 0` (no residual output on the success path).

**Gap 3 — per-branch weakness of the targeted test (criticality 3).** `internal/hook/generate_agents_test.go:754,758`. `Contains(..., "exit 2")` / `Contains(..., "head -n 60 &gt;&amp;2")` match one occurrence and cannot detect a single-branch revert; add a `NotContains(content, "exit $_rc")` to explicitly forbid the old exit form (complements the existing `NotContains` for the `2&gt;&amp;1 | head` masking form at line 765).

## Positive observations

- The four exact-string blocks are strong anti-drift pins and cover all three branches with the new pattern; a wholesale or single-branch textual revert fails immediately.
- The existing negative assertion `NotContains(content, "make check) 2&gt;&amp;1 | head")` (line 765) correctly guards against reintroducing the pipe-masking form.
- The renamed test name and updated comment (lines 736-741) accurately describe the intended contract, improving DAMP readability over the old "propagates make check exit code."
- `internal/hook/subprocess_test.go` already demonstrates the package can run emitted hook commands under a real shell, so closing Gap 1 requires no new test scaffolding pattern.

<summary>Agent "Silent-failure review of hook fix" finished</summary>
<note>A task-notification fires each time this agent stops with no live background children of its own. The user can send it another message and resume it, so the same task-id may notify more than once.</note>
<result>## Verdict

The fix eliminates the stdout-only / raw-exit-code silent failure. All three make-check branches are now byte-identical in their failure handling, and the hook is confirmed `PostToolUse` (generate_agents.go:304), where exit 2 + stderr is the correct signal that hands the block reason back to the model. One residual issue survives the fix and is worth flagging.

### Answers to the three specific questions

**(1) Any make-check failure path that could still exit non-2 or emit only to stdout?** No. Decoding the generated command at generate_agents.go:368, all three make-check branches (no-jq, empty-path, extension-match) use the identical tail:

```sh
_out=$(cd "$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR" &amp;&amp; make check 2&gt;&amp;1); _rc=$?; \
if [ $_rc -ne 0 ]; then printf '%s\n' "$_out" | head -n 60 &gt;&amp;2; exit 2; fi; exit 0
```

Failure → stderr (`&gt;&amp;2`) + `exit 2`; success → silent `exit 0`. No divergence between branches. The two non-check branches (`*/.tmp/*|.punt-labs/ethos/*` skip and the `*)` default) exit 0 by design and never run make check, so there is nothing to surface. Confirmed clean.

**(2) Does silent success mask anything that used to be visible and mattered?** No. Under the old form, success piped `head -n 60` of make-check output to stdout and exited 0. For a `PostToolUse` hook, exit-0 stdout is not fed to the model — it only surfaces in transcript mode. That output was make-check's success chatter (build/lint/test progress), which carries no actionable signal. Dropping it loses no signal a reviewer or the model needed.

**(3) Is exit 2 correct, and can `[ $_rc -ne 0 ]` miss a real failure?** Exit 2 is correct — for `PostToolUse`, exit 2 is the code that routes stderr back to the model as automated feedback. `_rc` cannot be unset: `_rc=$?` runs unconditionally on the same line immediately after the `_out=$(...)` assignment, and `$?` always holds the exit status of that command substitution. Signal death is caught: a make-check killed by a signal yields status 128+N (non-zero) → `exit 2`. A `cd` failure (bad/empty `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR`) short-circuits the `&amp;&amp;`, leaving a non-zero `_rc` → `exit 2` with the cd error captured via `2&gt;&amp;1` — a surfaced block, not a silent pass. No real failure escapes the `-ne 0` test.

Also verified safe: `_rc` is captured *before* the pipe to `head`, so SIGPIPE from `head` closing the pipe cannot overwrite it; and `printf '%s\n' "$_out"` treats `$_out` purely as data (no format-string interpretation of the captured output).

### Finding — MEDIUM

**Location:** internal/hook/generate_agents.go:368 (all three make-check branches; same in the old code)

**Issue:** The failure output is truncated with `head -n 60` — the *first* 60 lines. `make check` expands to `go vet` → `staticcheck` → `shellcheck` → `markdownlint` → `go test -race` → `validate-content`. Make stops at the first failing target, so the diagnostic that explains the failure is at the *end* of the accumulated output, not the start. When earlier successful stages (or a verbose `go test` run) produce more than ~60 lines before the failing tool's message, `head -n 60` emits 60 lines of passing-step noise to stderr and truncates the actual error away. The model receives a block with exit 2 but a reason that may not contain the failure.

**User/model impact:** This partially re-creates the very problem the PR fixes: the block fires, but the *reason handed to the model* can be uninformative. The agent sees "blocked" plus unrelated leading output, and cannot tell what to fix — the debugging signal is still lost, just via truncation instead of misrouting.

**Recommendation:** Switch the truncation from `head -n 60` to `tail -n 60` in all three branches so the failing tool's output (which make emits last) is preserved. This is the same edit already applied uniformly, so keeping the branches identical is trivial. Note this is a change from the existing behavior, not introduced by this PR — but it directly determines whether the fix's stated goal ("the failure reason is visible") actually holds. Flagging rather than modifying per instructions.

No other high-confidence findings. The escaping in the `fmt.Fprintf` format string matches the three test expectations verbatim (generate_agents_test.go:210, 391, 420, 730), and the `%%s`/`%s` distinction (literal `%s` for printf vs. the `filePatterns` substitution) is correct.</result>
<usage><subagent_tokens>65676</subagent_tokens><tool_uses>6</tool_uses><duration_ms>116826</duration_ms></usage>
</task-notification>

[assistant] silent-failure-hunter found a sharp MEDIUM that's directly on-point: `head -n 60` keeps the **first** 60 lines, but `make check` stops at the first failing target and the diagnostic lands at the **end** of the accumulated output. So on a failure with >60 lines of passing-stage noise first, the actual error gets truncated away — partially recreating the bug we're fixing. Fix: `tail -n 60` in all 3 branches. Per the no-"pre-existing" rule and because it decides whether the fix's goal actually holds, I'm folding this in.

2. **behavioral test** (pr-test-analyzer, crit 7) — add an execution test that runs the emitted command with a stub `make` and asserts exit 2 + stderr on failure, exit 0 + silence on success.

<result>Verified everything against the source. Here are my findings.

## Summary

The original criticality-7 gap is **CLOSED**. `TestPostToolUseHook_Execution` genuinely executes the emitted hook command as a real `/bin/sh` subprocess and asserts exit-code and stream behavior that no text match could prove. I confirmed this both by reading and by mutation testing: inverting `-ne 0` to `-eq 0` in the source fails the test (both subtests), and the change is otherwise clean.

## Point-by-point confirmation

**(1) Does it actually EXECUTE, not string-match? YES.**
`runHook` (`internal/hook/generate_agents_exec_test.go:115-136`) runs `exec.Command("/bin/sh", "-c", command)` where `command` is the real emitted hook string parsed out of the generated `bwk.md` frontmatter (`extractPostToolUseCommand`, lines 69-99). Stdin, stdout, stderr, and exit code are captured from the live process. This is execution, not `strings.Contains`.

**(2) Case A — failing make → exit 2, stderr has output, stdout empty? YES.**
Lines 45-54: stub make emits a marker then `exit 1`. Asserts `code == 2` (line 51), `stderr` contains the marker (line 52), `stdout` empty (line 53). All three hold.

**(3) Case B — passing make → exit 0 and BOTH streams empty? YES.**
Lines 56-64: stub make is `exit 0`. Asserts `code == 0` (line 61), `stdout` empty (line 62), `stderr` empty (line 63).

**(4) Hermetic? YES.**
`t.TempDir()` for both the project root (`setupTestRepo`) and the stub-make dir (`stubMake`, line 107); `CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR` set to a fresh `t.TempDir()` (line 121); PATH has `binDir` prepended (line 120) so the stub `make` wins over any real one. No real Makefile, no network. Host-independence of the jq-vs-no-jq split is handled: the `internal/foo.go` path routes to the make-check branch in both the jq `*.go` case and the no-jq unconditional branch (documented lines 39-42), so the outcome does not depend on whether jq is installed on the runner. Verified by the passing run.

**(5) Would it catch the three regressions?**
- **Logic inversion (`-eq 0` vs `-ne 0`): YES — proven.** I mutated all `-ne 0` to `-eq 0` in `generate_agents.go` and ran the test: both subtests failed (failure case gave exit 0 / empty stderr; success case gave exit 2 / non-empty stderr). Source restored, `git diff` clean.
- **Broken if/fi nesting: YES.** A malformed conditional makes `/bin/sh -c` a parse error — exit code ≠ 2 and ≠ 0 with syntax noise on stderr — breaking both subtests' assertions.
- **head-vs-tail regression: NO, not by this behavioral test.** This is the one residual gap (see below).

**(6) Remaining gap — head/tail is not behaviorally exercised (low criticality, ~3).**
The failure stub emits a single line (`"echo "+marker+"\nexit 1\n"`, line 47). On one line of output, `head -n 60` and `tail -n 60` are identical, so this test cannot distinguish them. A `tail`→`head` revert is caught only by the text-pinning assertions in `generate_agents_test.go` (line 751, `assert.Contains(t, content, "tail -n 60 &gt;&amp;2")`, plus the four full-command literals). That is adequate coverage, but note the guarantee is textual, not behavioral: if someone reverted `tail`→`head` and updated the string assertion in tandem (exactly the pattern this PR used in reverse), nothing behavioral would catch it. To close fully, the failure stub could emit 70+ numbered lines and assert the stderr contains the last line but not the first. Not a merge blocker — the head→tail fix is the raison d'être of commit `60660c3` and is text-pinned.

Minor: only the Go-pattern `*.go` branch of `bwk.md` is executed. The generic-fallback branch, the `.tmp/` skip branch, and the no-jq branch are text-pinned but never run. Optional; criticality ~2.

## Sanity check: head→tail source change

Correct. `make check` runs targets sequentially and stops at the first failure; with combined output captured to `_out`, the failing target's diagnostic lands at the *end* of the accumulated text. `head -n 60` would keep the first 60 lines (early `go vet`/`staticcheck` preamble) and truncate the actual error; `tail -n 60` keeps the diagnostic. The updated code comments (`generate_agents.go:355-368`) and both emitted `command` strings switch `head`→`tail` consistently, and all four text assertions in `generate_agents_test.go` plus the `tail -n 60 &gt;&amp;2` marker assertion were updated to match. Full test run passes (`TestGenerateAgentFiles`, `TestPostToolUseHook_Execution`, and the project-patterns suite all green).

## Verdict

Original criticality-7 gap: **CLOSED**. The behavioral test executes the emitted command and asserts exit-code semantics (2 on block, 0 on pass) and stream routing (stderr on failure, both empty on success) — precisely the properties the text-pinning tests could not verify, and it demonstrably catches the logic inversion that motivated the concern. One low-value residual (head/tail is text-pinned, not behaviorally exercised) is worth a follow-up note but does not block merge.

## Reviewing

Round-2 changes on `fix/ethos-bo84-hook-stderr-exit2`, diff `bea460e..HEAD`:

- `CHANGELOG.md`

## Findings

No high-confidence findings. Each of the five focus points verified positive.

**(1) head→tail consistency — verified.** `generate_agents.go:371` contains exactly 3 `tail -n 60` occurrences (the no-jq branch, the empty-`$_path` branch, and the `%s`-pattern case branch) and zero `head -n 60`. The comment at `generate_agents.go:332` and `358-362` was updated to match, including the new rationale (make stops at first failing target → error is at end of output). The four pinned-string assertions in `generate_agents_test.go` (lines 210, 391, 420, 730) all updated to `tail`, and the stderr-routing assertion at `generate_agents_test.go:754` now asserts `tail -n 60 &gt;&amp;2`. Pinned strings match generator output — `TestGenerateAgentFiles` passes.

**(2) NotContains masking guard — correct, intentionally references `head`.** `generate_agents_test.go:765-767` still asserts the command does NOT contain `` `make check) 2&gt;&amp;1 | head` ``. This guards against regressing to the old un-captured masking form (`(cd … &amp;&amp; make check) 2&gt;&amp;1 | head`), which is distinct from the current capture-then-`tail` form. Leaving it as `head` is correct — it was not blindly flipped to `tail`. The string can never appear in the current command regardless (the current form is `make check 2&gt;&amp;1)` inside `$(...)`), so the guard is a valid regression tripwire.

**(3) New exec test — correct, hermetic, no flakiness.** Build tag `//go:build linux || darwin` is correct (uses `/bin/sh`, excludes Windows). Hermetic: `t.TempDir()` project dir, `stubMake` on a prepended PATH via `t.TempDir()`, `CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR` pointed at a fresh empty temp dir — no reliance on the real Makefile. Robust to jq presence/absence: `internal/foo.go` routes to `make check` both when jq is present (`*.go` case matches) and absent (no-jq branch runs unconditionally); I confirmed jq is present locally and the test passed 5/5 runs (`-count=5`) with no flakiness. `go vet` clean.

**(4) `exec.Command("/bin/sh","-c",command)` — not an injection risk.** `command` is the generator-produced hook string extracted from the agent file, and `stdin` is a fixed test literal. No external/user input flows into the shell. Executing the real generated command under the real interpreter is the point of the test — it catches logic inversions, `if/fi` nesting, and dash incompatibilities that a text match cannot. Safe.

**(5) Go correctness — none found.** `runHook` returns `code=0` by default on `err==nil` (success) and extracts the code from `*exec.ExitError` on failure, with `require.ErrorAs` failing loudly on a non-exit error (e.g., failed to start). `extractPostToolUseCommand` slices the first `\n---\n` (the frontmatter close, unambiguous since frontmatter YAML holds no `---` lines) and relies on `yaml.Unmarshal` to undo YAML escaping — the correct way to recover the literal command. `require`/`assert` usage and struct tags are correct.

One observation, not a finding: the `NotContains(command, "exit $_rc")` guard at `generate_agents_exec_test.go:44` and the `NotContains(content, "make check) 2&gt;&amp;1 | head")` guard at `generate_agents_test.go:765` overlap in intent (both guard the masking regression) but check different literal forms — this is defensible redundancy, not a defect.</result>

[user] <!-- markdownlint-disable MD041 -->

## Input

Arguments: clear

Parse as one of three modes:

1. **Clear**: if arguments are exactly `clear` → call with `clear=True`
2. **Post with duration**: if the last token matches a duration pattern (`30m`, `2h`, `1d`, `3d`), it is the duration and everything before it is the message → `message="...", duration="2h"`
3. **Post with default**: otherwise the entire argument string is the message → `message="..."`

If no arguments are provided, call with no parameters (shows current wall).

Examples:

- `release freeze — do not push to main` → `message="release freeze — do not push to main"`
- `deploy window open 2h` → `message="deploy window open"`, `duration="2h"`
- `clear` → `clear=true`
- (empty) → no parameters

## Task

Call `mcp__plugin_biff_tty__wall` with the parsed values. The result is already formatted by a PostToolUse hook and displayed above. Do not repeat or reformat the data. Do not send any text after the tool call.

[assistant] Investigation changes the picture — this is **systemic, not ethos-specific**, and touches sensitive shared infra:

- ethos is `dolt_mode: server` (central Hosted DoltDB is the source of truth), yet **15 files of the local Dolt working copy** (`.beads/dolt/.dolt/` — `manifest`, `sql-server.info`, `noms/LOCK`, `repo_state.json`, …) are committed.
- **Every repo does this** — quarry tracks the same 15. So the local Dolt runtime being committed is an org-wide beads-setup pattern, and a live dolt server rewrites those files, dirtying the tree on every session.

The fix is the right instinct — gitignore `.beads/dolt/` runtime + `git rm --cached` — but it's **org-wide and carries a real risk I shouldn't guess on**: the `.beads/.gitignore` is deliberately configured with stern warnings, and I can't yet confirm whether a fresh clone needs the committed `.beads/dolt/` skeleton to bootstrap the local server, or whether it self-inits from the remote. If it bootstraps from the commit, untracking breaks `bd` on clone across every repo.

Because this is shared beads infrastructure with cross-repo blast radius, I'm not going to unilaterally untrack it. My recommendation: **delegate the org-wide fix to adb** (infra/CI owner) — determine whether `.beads/dolt/` is bootstrap-required, then either gitignore+untrack the runtime subset or the whole dir, and roll it into the canonical `.beads/.gitignore` template across all repos.

[assistant] This is actually **Jim's request** (bead owner jmf-pobox, "Requested by Jim 2026-07-11"), surfaced via vox — not just an FYI. Two capabilities:
1. **Repo-primary/authoritative resolution** — resolve from `.punt-labs/ethos/` first, opt-in per repo, so a global-less checkout works and the vendored set wins.
2. **Complete-vendor command** — a non-lossy `ethos vendor` to snapshot a complete resolvable set (transitive deps + `.ext`) into the repo, since `ethos export` drops data.

Let me ground this against the actual resolution design (DES-051 three-layer) before I opine, then reply to vox and bring you the assessment.

[user] [tool_result] Command running in background with ID: bovs2ooez. Output is being written to: /private/tmp/claude-501/-Users-jfreeman-Coding-punt-labs-ethos/1f33d677-8e9d-4614-9d73-fb7c4909a480/tasks/bovs2ooez.output. You will be notified when it completes. To check interim output, use Read on that file path.

[assistant] Grounded now. The architecture confirms the gap precisely: the resolver is **repo-local → active bundle → global** (DES-051), where "repo-local overrides win, **global fallback catches the tail**." That tail-fallback is exactly why `ylc` (global-only) still resolves against a vendored repo. So the two asks map cleanly:

1. **Repo-authoritative mode** — a new opt-in knob (in `.punt-labs/ethos.yaml`) that *disables the global fallback*, so the repo layer is the sole, complete source. Repo-local-**first** already exists; this is repo-local-**only**.
2. **`ethos vendor`** — walk the full transitive closure (identity → personality/writing-style/talents/roles/teams **+ `.ext/` dirs** that `ethos export` drops) and snapshot a complete resolvable set into `.punt-labs/ethos/`.

Complementary: vendor makes the copy complete; repo-authoritative makes it sufficient. <result>Design written to `/Users/jfreeman/Coding/punt-labs/ethos/docs/ni0y-resolution-mode.md`. Not committed, no branch — as instructed.

## Recommendations

**Config knob:** a string enum `resolution` in `.punt-labs/ethos.yaml`, sibling to `active_bundle`, allowed values `layered` (default, unset = today byte-identical) and `repo-only`. Unknown value is a hard error at config load. Rejected `vendored: true` (conflates provenance with policy) and `global_fallback: false` (negative-boolean footgun). Added to `RepoConfig` at `internal/resolve/resolve.go:29`, with a `ResolveResolution` resolver.

**Store mechanism:** one read-time policy — a `repoAuthoritative bool` threaded into all four `NewLayeredStoreWithBundle` constructors. It gates only the global *read* branch; writes and extensions still target global (DES-044 preserved). For identity/role/team it guards the global tail (`identity/layered.go:93,212,217,219,341,352,304`; `role/layered.go:70`; `team/layered.go:67`). For the attribute store, which is built global-at-top with a `fallback` chain (`attribute/layered.go:42-49`), it changes construction so global is absent from the chain. One injection point: `identityStore()` (`cmd/ethos/identity.go:28`) reads the policy once; the derived role/team/attribute builders and every hook/MCP surface inherit it.

**active_bundle interaction:** repo-only drops global only, keeping repo → bundle when the bundle is repo-local (`SourceRepo`) or legacy (`SourceLegacy`) — both travel with the checkout. A global-scoped bundle (`SourceGlobal`) under repo-only is contradictory and fails at startup in `resolveBundleRoot`.

**Miss-behavior contract:** aggregate all misses, return one typed error (`ErrIncompleteRepoSet` wrapping `[]MissingRef{Kind,Slug,Path}`) listing the handle plus each missing `{kind}/{slug}.md`. Referenced-but-missing attributes, today soft warnings (`identity/layered.go:168,180,189`), become hard errors in repo-only mode. Surfaces: whoami (exit non-zero), agent generation (fail the affected agent), session start (stderr + skip injection, recommended over abort), MCP (typed error per DES-020), and a new `ethos doctor` completeness check as the authoritative gate.

**Vendor coupling (mdm):** repo-only is the verify half; vendor is the produce half. Vendor must guarantee a complete reference closure (identities → attributes → roles/teams, no dangling refs) and refuse to write `resolution: repo-only` until it validates. Shared artifact: the typed completeness check — vendor calls it before writing the mode, doctor calls it to gate, the stores raise it on a live miss. Ship vendor first or same release.

## Open questions for the leader
1. Session-start miss: degrade (stderr + skip injection) or abort? Recommend degrade, doctor as hard gate.
2. Attribute write routing in repo-only: route writes to the repo (recommended) or keep global-targeted and accept a create-then-invisible footgun?
3. Confirm the key name `resolution: repo-only` before implementation, since the vendor design writes the same key.

The proposed ADR (Problem/Decision/Reasoning/Rejected alternatives/Implications, number left as DES-0NN) is in §6, matching DESIGN.md house style.</result>

**Both designs are strong and cite code.** The two halves interlock cleanly — vendor's completeness postcondition is exactly repo-only mode's precondition.

**Decision points forming (I'll bring these with the reviewers' verdicts):**
1. **Config key** — `resolution: layered | repo-only` in `.punt-labs/ethos.yaml` (unset = today, byte-identical).
2. **They must ship together** — extensions currently resolve from global *only*, so a vendored `.ext/` is dead weight until repo-only mode reads ext from the repo. One release, not two.
3. **⚠️ Security — `.ext/` secrets:** `.ext/` holds things like GPG key IDs / tokens and is untracked global state; `ethos vendor` copying it into a *git-tracked* `.punt-labs/ethos/` could commit consumer secrets. mdm flags this as needing safe-by-default handling — I'll likely want a **djb security pass** on the vendor design before we implement.
4. **Smaller calls** — session-start miss behavior (degrade vs abort), whether vendor clears `active_bundle`, and scope (identities-only vs also repo config/missions/pipelines).

I'll reconcile both designs + both evaluations into a single DES-0NN ADR and come back with a crisp decision list — no implementation dispatches until you've ruled. Standing by for the evaluators.

<summary>Agent "Evaluate resolution-mode design" finished</summary>
<note>A task-notification fires each time this agent stops with no live background children of its own. The user can send it another message and resume it, so the same task-id may notify more than once.</note>
<result>Verdict and findings below. I read the design in full and verified every load-bearing file:line claim against the code.

## Verdict: APPROVE-WITH-CHANGES

The design is sound in shape and mostly accurate in its code claims. The config knob (string enum), the ADR with rejected alternatives, the miss-behavior contract (aggregated typed error), and the active_bundle interaction are all correct and complete. Every material file:line citation checks out (loadRaw `layered.go:93`, attrChain `212/217/219`, FindBy `341`, Exists `352`, List `304`, role `70`, team `67`, attribute chain `layered.go:42-49`, `resolveBundleRoot` legacy `""` at `bundle.go:31`, single injection through `identityStore()`, `doctor.RunAll` receiving the layered store at `main.go:219`). The one imprecision is trivial: the attribute-warning citations should be `169/178/189`, not `168/180/189` (off by one to two lines — points at the `if err` line, not the `append`).

But there are six design-time gaps, all cheaper to fix in the doc than to discover in implementation. Ranked.

### 1. Write routing is inconsistent across the four stores — the write-then-invisible footgun is broader than the design admits (top finding)

The design (§2) keeps identity/role/team writes targeting **global** ("Writes and extensions still target global") but flips attribute writes to **repo** (§2 attribute construction: "reads and writes target the vendored set"). It then raises the write-then-invisible problem *only for attributes* in open question 2.

That is the worst of both worlds. In repo-only mode as designed:
- `ethos talent create foo` → writes to repo → visible to repo-only reads.
- `ethos identity create foo` → `writeStore()` returns global (`identity/layered.go:510`), `Save` writes global → **invisible** to repo-only reads. `ethos whoami` for `foo` then fails "not found in repo-only" against a handle you just created.

Same for role `Save` (`role/layered.go:44` → global) and team `Save` (`team/layered.go:44` → global). The footgun the design flags for attributes applies with equal force to three stores it leaves on global, and it is silent about them.

Recommendation: pick one uniform policy. In repo-only, route **all** writes to the repo layer (consistent with reads, no invisible-write class). This resolves open question 2 and extends the decision to the three stores the design under-scopes. If the leader prefers writes-stay-global, then attributes must too — but do not ship the split.

### 2. whoami cannot produce the promised repo-only diagnostic

§4's table says whoami prints "the missing list to stderr." It can't. whoami resolves via `resolve.Resolve` → `store.FindBy("github"/…)` (`resolve.go:62,74,86`). With the global branch gated, `FindBy` returns `(nil, nil)` on no repo match, so `Resolve` falls through all three probes and returns the generic `"no identity matches git user %q, email %q, or OS user %q"` (`resolve.go:95`) — it never knew which handle to name, so it cannot say "`claudia` not found; global fallback disabled."

The nice §4 identity-miss message only fires for an explicit `Load("claudia")`, not for self-resolution. Design-time fix: specify that `Resolve`'s terminal no-match error is wrapped with a repo-only hint when the policy is active ("no repo-local identity matches; `resolution: repo-only` disables the global fallback"). Otherwise the most common operator-facing surface gives a confusing generic error.

### 3. repo-only is silently ignored when there is no repo ethos layer

`identityStore()` early-returns the plain global `*identity.Store` when `repoRoot == "" &amp;&amp; bundleRoot == ""` (`identity.go:32-34`). That store is not a `LayeredStore` and has no `repoAuthoritative` concept. A repo with `.punt-labs/ethos.yaml` containing `resolution: repo-only` but no `.punt-labs/ethos/` directory and no repo-local bundle would resolve **everything from global** — the exact tail the mode exists to remove, silently. Note also the config lives at `.punt-labs/ethos.yaml` (keyed off `FindRepoRoot`) while the repo store layer is keyed off `FindRepoEthosRoot` — the two can disagree.

Design-time fix: specify that `resolution: repo-only` with no repo layer and no repo-local/legacy bundle is a **hard startup error**, not a fall-through to global. State it as an invariant next to the §3 global-bundle rejection.

### 4. Five read paths to gate, not four stores — the identity store has two independent global surfaces

The design frames this as "one policy threaded uniformly," but the mechanism is not uniform, and the identity store carries **two** independent global reads: identity lookup (`loadRaw`/`FindBy`/`Exists`/`List`) *and* attribute resolution, which runs a **separate** chain (`attrChain` → `loadAttribute`, building a fresh `attribute.NewStore` per layer at `identity/layered.go:225-226`) that is not the fallback-chained `attribute.Store`. Meanwhile the attribute store used by `ethos talent/personality/writing-style` CRUD is gated by a *construction* change, not a guard. That is three distinct gating mechanisms across five read surfaces. The design covers all of them, but by describing it as one uniform boolean it invites an implementer to gate `loadRaw` and miss `attrChain`, or gate the attribute construction and miss the identity-internal attribute chain. Call the five surfaces out explicitly in §2 as a checklist.

### 5. Attribute construction snippet has an ordering bug and a nil-deref

The §2 attribute snippet must be placed **before** the existing early return at `attribute/layered.go:28-30` (`if repoRoot == "" &amp;&amp; bundleRoot == "" { return NewStore(globalRoot, kind) }`) — otherwise repo-only with empty roots still returns a global-only store. And `top := repo` dereferences a nil `*Store` when `repoRoot == ""` (repo is nil). Both are the same root cause as finding 3: specify that repo-only requires a non-nil repo (or repo-local bundle) layer, and guard it.

### 6. Pin the owning package for the shared completeness check

§4/§7 make the typed completeness check (`ErrIncompleteRepoSet` + closure walk) the shared artifact between three callers: the stores (live miss), `ethos doctor` (gate), and `ethos vendor` (mdm's separate mission, pre-write validation). §4 tentatively locates the type in `identity.ErrIncompleteRepoSet`, but the *closure walk* (identity → attributes → roles → teams → collaboration graph, per §7) is broader than the identity package and will be imported by both doctor and vendor. Burying it in `identity` risks vendor reimplementing it. Design-time fix: name the owning package for the closure-check function (recommend a neutral `internal/vendor` or the doctor check both call), and state it in both this design and the vendor design so the two missions converge on one implementation. This is the one cross-mission coordination risk worth flagging to the leader before either dispatches.

## On bwk's three open questions

1. **Session-start degrade vs abort** — Agree: **degrade** (stderr + skip injection), `doctor` as the hard gate. A missing persona attribute must not brick a live Claude session; the operator runs `doctor` deliberately to catch incompleteness. Sound.
2. **Attribute write routing** — Route to **repo**, but do not stop at attributes: make it uniform across all four stores (finding 1). The recommendation is right; its scope is too narrow.
3. **Config key name `resolution: repo-only`** — Agree. String enum over boolean is the correct call: room for future modes, no negative-boolean footgun, reads cleanly in diffs and diagnostics, and the vendor design references the same key. Confirm before either mission implements.

## What holds without change

- **DES-044 preservation** is sound: gating only the global *read* leaves extensions on global (`Load` ext at `layered.go:55`, `ExtSet`/`writeStore` untouched). The DES-044 invariant itself is not at risk — the write-then-invisible problem (finding 1) is a *different, broader* issue that the design incorrectly narrows to attributes.
- **active_bundle interaction** (§3) is correct and safe: drop the global tail, keep repo→bundle for `SourceRepo`/`SourceLegacy`, reject `SourceGlobal` at startup. Matches `ResolveActive` returning `Source` (`bundle/resolve.go:29`) and the fatal-startup pattern in `resolveBundleRoot`.
- **Back-compat when unset** is genuinely byte-identical: two-arg wrappers pass `false`, every guard is `if repoAuthoritative`, and the attribute early-return path is unchanged. The only caveat is finding 3 — "unset" is safe; "set but no repo layer" is the unspecified path.

Relevant files: `/Users/jfreeman/Coding/punt-labs/ethos/docs/ni0y-resolution-mode.md` (the design under review); the gaps touch `/Users/jfreeman/Coding/punt-labs/ethos/cmd/ethos/identity.go:28-44`, `/Users/jfreeman/Coding/punt-labs/ethos/internal/identity/layered.go:44-65,150-222,510`, `/Users/jfreeman/Coding/punt-labs/ethos/internal/attribute/layered.go:27-50`, and `/Users/jfreeman/Coding/punt-labs/ethos/internal/resolve/resolve.go:45-96`.</result>
<usage><subagent_tokens>82363</subagent_tokens><tool_uses>16</tool_uses><duration_ms>193742</duration_ms></usage>
</task-notification>

[assistant] rsc's verdict on the resolution design: **APPROVE-WITH-CHANGES** — shape is sound, every file:line claim verified, but 6 design-time gaps worth fixing in the doc (all cheaper now than in code). The important ones:
- **Write-routing footgun is broader than bwk admitted** — identity/role/team writes still go to global (invisible in repo-only), only attributes flip to repo. Fix: route *all* writes to repo uniformly in repo-only mode.
- **`whoami` can't actually produce the "what's missing" diagnostic** as designed (falls through to a generic error) — needs the Resolve terminal error wrapped with a repo-only hint.
- **`resolution: repo-only` silently ignored** when a repo has the config but no repo ethos layer → resolves everything from global (the exact tail it's meant to kill). Must be a hard startup error.
- **Cross-mission risk:** the shared completeness-check needs a named owning package (not buried in `identity`) so vendor + doctor + the stores converge on one implementation — flagged explicitly for me to resolve before dispatch.

[user] [tool_result] No new messages.

[assistant] Here's the change in plain terms.

## The problem

Ethos stores identities (name, personality, writing style, talents, roles, team membership) in two places: a **global** registry on your machine (`~/.punt-labs/ethos/`, ~63 identities) and an optional **repo-local** copy (`.punt-labs/ethos/`).

When ethos looks up an identity, it checks repo-local first, then falls back to global. That fallback is the problem: **if a handle is missing from the repo copy, ethos silently pulls it from your global machine instead.**

vox tried to make itself self-contained by copying 15 identities into its repo. But it's not actually self-contained — `ylc` and `claudia` aren't in that copy, yet they still resolve because ethos quietly reaches into the global registry. On a fresh clone (a CI box, a new laptop, a teammate without your global home), those identities would just vanish, and nothing warns you. The repo *looks* portable but isn't.

## The fix — two halves

**1. `ethos vendor` (a new command).** Snapshots a *complete* identity set into the repo. "Complete" means it follows every reference — an identity needs its personality/writing-style/talents/roles, a team pulls in all its members (that's how `claudia` gets caught — she's only reachable through team membership), and it also copies the `.ext/` sidecar dirs that today's `ethos export` throws away. The result: a repo copy that resolves entirely on its own, no global needed.

**2. Repo-authoritative mode (an opt-in config flag).** A line in `.punt-labs/ethos.yaml` — `resolution: repo-only` — that **turns off the global fallback**. Now the repo copy is the *only* source. If something's missing, ethos fails loudly and tells you exactly which identity and which files are absent, instead of silently borrowing from global.

## Why both

They're two sides of one guarantee. Vendor *produces* a complete set; repo-only mode *proves* it's complete by refusing to paper over gaps. Vox's current 15-identity copy (missing `ylc`/`claudia`) is the acceptance test: run `ethos vendor` → get a complete set; flip on `repo-only` → it resolves with zero global fallback, or hard-errors listing exactly what's missing.

## Practical impact

- **Default is unchanged** — if you don't set `resolution: repo-only`, ethos behaves exactly as today. This is opt-in per repo.
- It's what lets a repo be genuinely portable/publishable — clone it anywhere and the agent identities resolve without depending on whatever's on the local machine.
- **One caveat I'm watching:** vendoring copies `.ext/` sidecars, which can hold secrets (GPG key IDs, tokens), into a *git-tracked* dir — so vendor needs to be safe-by-default (skip/redact secrets) to avoid committing them. That's the main thing I'll want a security look at before we build it.

It's dev/agent-identity infrastructure, not a runtime dependency of shipped products — so it's a portability/publish-readiness improvement, not a bug fix. Want me to go deeper on either half, or keep reconciling the designs into the ADR?

## Verdict: APPROVE-WITH-CHANGES

The design is sound. All five success criteria are met. The closure algorithm is correct and terminating, and the reverse `identity→team` edge is correctly identified as the load-bearing insight. The changes below are refinements, not corrections of a broken design — but F1 and F2 are cheaper to settle now than in implementation.

## Citation audit

All substantive claims verified accurate: `export.go:20` (lossy contract), `identity.go:16-18` (attribute edges), `team.go:16-19` (member edges), `team.go:110-114` (collab→filled-role), `role.go:28-36` (roles are leaves — confirmed no outward identity/attribute edges), `ext.go:28/36-38`, `layered.go:54-55` and `479-482` (ext resolves global-only), `layered.go:93` (global fallback), `cmd/ethos/identity.go:30-43`, `resolve.go:138`, `bundle/resolve.go:64-74` (SourceLegacy), `team_bundle.go:517`.

One citation is wrong — see F4.

## Answers to the seven assessment points

1. **Closure correctness.** Edge set is complete for the resolution graph. Roles are leaves (`role.go:28-36`: Model/Responsibilities/Permissions/Tools/SafetyConstraints/OutputFormat — none reference identities, attributes, or other roles). No team→team edge exists. Collaborations reference only member-filled roles (`team.go:110-114`), adding no nodes. The reverse edge is correctly load-bearing: without it, global-only teammates (`claudia`) are dropped. **Termination is guaranteed** — finite node universe, monotone set growth, fixed point per the outer loop. One missed edge, low severity: the `agent` field (`identity.go:15`) — see F7.

2. **Completeness guarantee.** The §9 predicate is precise and testable, and maps 1:1 onto bwk's repo-only resolution — it is a usable precondition. Verifying by constructing a repo-only store and running the actual resolution is the right move (it dogfoods the exact mechanism). Caveat in F8: the ext clause can only be verified as file-presence until bwk's read-side lands.

3. **`.ext/` secrets (OQ3).** Serious. This is my top finding — see F1. `--no-ext` (opt-out) is the wrong polarity; default must be safe-by-default (opt-in).

4. **export vs vendor.** Keep both. Correct call. Genuinely different jobs (foreign-format lossy handoff vs native lossless closure); "vendor" is the established term for exactly this. §6 table disambiguates cleanly. No confusion.

5. **Command surface.** Top-level `ethos vendor` is right (a team is one entry point to the closure, not the operation's subject). But the flag set is over-built — see F2. Two flags let the user defeat the tool's one job.

6. **MCP + DES-020.** Adequately specified (schema, `VendorResult`, `formatVendor` mirroring `formatTeam`), modulo the file-location error (F4) and a polarity inconsistency (F6).

7. **Coupling/ordering.** mdm's "must ship together" is too strong if F1 is adopted — see F5. Only the ext dimension is coupled to bwk; the core closure is independently shippable and verifiable.

## Ranked findings

**F1 — HIGH, cheaper in design. Flip `.ext/` to safe-by-default (opt-in), not opt-out.** Global ext is untracked, mode `0o600` (`ext.go:140` writes `0o600`) — a signal it may hold secrets. DES-008 means ethos cannot distinguish a token from a prose hint, so it cannot safely auto-commit ext into git-tracked `.punt-labs/ethos/`. Critically, ext is **not required for the completeness predicate**: `Load` succeeds with no ext (`layered.go:55-56` — ext is additive, never causes not-found). And ext is inert until bwk's read-side (OQ1). So defaulting ext OFF costs nothing on the core guarantee and removes the exposure. The marquee `claudia` case is served by the reverse team edge + attribute closure (writing-styles/personalities), not by ext. Recommend: default off, `--include-ext` opt-in, djb signs off on a redaction policy before enabling. mdm's success criterion "the `.ext` dirs that export drops" is still satisfied — ext handling is specified (§4), just not default-on.

**F2 — HIGH/MED, cheaper in design, minimalism. Cut the flags that defeat completeness.** The doc itself admits (§2 caveats) that `--no-teams` and `--from global|bundle` produce snapshots that are **not complete**. A command whose single job is "complete self-standing snapshot" should not ship flags that break the invariant. Cut `--no-teams` (following the reverse edge *is* what complete means). Drop `--from` for v1 (single-layer extraction is a different operation — YAGNI). Reconsider `--no-clobber` for v1 (idempotent sync per §5 makes it an edge case). Survivors: `[handle...] --team --all --to --prune --dry-run --json`. Nine down to seven, and no survivor can produce a false "complete."

**F3 — MED, correctness/expectation. State the closure blast radius.** The §9 predicate forces the entire connected component of the team graph: once `claudia ∈ D`, every team containing her must be in `D`, pulling teammates-of-teammates transitively. In a densely-connected org, `ethos vendor claude` vendors most of the roster. This is a true closure and self-consistent, but the "6 identities" example undersells it. Recommend: document the blast radius and make `--dry-run` the recommended first step. (Do not add a bounded mode — completeness demands the full closure.)

**F4 — MED, factual error, cheaper in design. Wrong package for the formatter.** §7 says `internal/mcp/format_output.go` and cites `format_output.go:61-80`. The switch is at **`internal/hook/format_output.go:61-80`** (verified — the formatter is a PostToolUse hook, not colocated with the MCP tool defs). `formatVendor` goes in `internal/hook/format_output.go`; the tool definition (`vendor_tools.go`) goes in `internal/mcp/`. Line numbers are right; the package is wrong. Fix so the implementer looks in the right place.

**F5 — MED, release risk. Coupling claim is too strong if F1 is adopted.** OQ1 says vendor + repo-mode must ship together. True only for ext. The core closure (identities/attributes/roles/teams) is independently verifiable **today** via a bare repo-only store (`identity.NewStore(D)`, no layering resolves repo-only) and independently useful. With ext opt-in-off (F1), vendor's core ships and self-verifies standalone; ext-vendoring + bwk's repo-mode ext-read + djb's redaction ship together later. Lower release risk. If ext stays default-on, mdm's coupling claim stands — so this finding is contingent on F1.

**F6 — LOW, consistency. Plan/write polarity mismatch.** CLI writes by default (`--dry-run` opt-out); the MCP tool defaults `method` to `plan` (§7); `team migrate` is plan-by-default (`--apply` to execute, `team_bundle.go:517-524`). Pick one polarity for CLI and MCP. Writes land in git-tracked space, which argues plan-by-default; "a sync you re-run" argues write-by-default. Leader's call — just make the two surfaces agree.

**F7 — LOW, predicate gap. The `agent` field is unaddressed.** `identity.go:15` `Agent` points to an agent `.md`. The closure and §9 ignore it. Agent files are generated artifacts (hook package), so out of scope is defensible — but say so explicitly, as the doc does for repo config (OQ4) and non-identity content (OQ5). One line: agent `.md` is regenerated, not vendored.

**F8 — LOW, verification caveat.** §9 claims vendor verifies completeness "as its final step" and `Complete: true` means repo-only resolution is safe. For the ext dimension this is unverifiable until bwk's repo-mode reads ext (OQ1) — vendor can check ext *files exist*, not that resolution *consults* them. State the predicate's ext clause as file-presence-only until the read-side lands. Ties to F1/F5.

## Rulings on the open questions

- **OQ1 (ext read-side, "blocking"):** Real (`layered.go:54-55`, `479-482`). Adopt F1 and it drops from blocking-for-vendor to prerequisite-for-ext-vendoring, which ships later. Not blocking for vendor core.
- **OQ2 (active-bundle):** Repo wins regardless (verified `identity.go:36-43` construction + `layered.go:72-97` load order). Recommend: vendor does not touch config, but warns if `active_bundle` is set — a self-standing repo intends no competing layer. Operator ruling fine; low stakes.
- **OQ3 (ext secrets):** See F1 — flip to opt-in, djb signs off before enabling. Sharpest issue.
- **OQ4 (repo config):** Agree — out of scope. Config stays hand-owned.
- **OQ5 (non-identity content):** Agree — out of scope. Correct boundary.

## Minimalism verdict

Nine flags is two too many, and the two extras (`--no-teams`, `--from`) are the ones that let a user produce an incomplete "complete" snapshot — the worst kind of flag. Cut them (F2). No flag should let the user defeat the tool's one job. The design's core — reverse-edge closure, verify-by-construction, native lossless layout, keep-both-verbs — is right.

Design doc reviewed: `/Users/jfreeman/Coding/punt-labs/ethos/docs/ni0y-vendor-command.md`. I made no edits (design review; leader decides).</result>

**1. `.ext/` secrets — the sharp one.** `.ext/` sidecars are untracked, `0600`-permissioned global state that can hold secrets (GPG key IDs, tokens). Copying them into a *git-tracked* `.punt-labs/ethos/` risks committing secrets. rop's key insight: **ext isn't needed for completeness** — the marquee `claudia` case is caught by the team-graph closure + writing-style/personality, not by ext; and ext is inert until the read-side lands anyway.

**2. Scope / sequencing.** With ext deferred (per #1), the two halves cleanly split:
- **v1 (now):** `ethos vendor` core (identities + attributes + roles + teams) + repo-authoritative mode — self-verifying, ships together, solves vox's actual case.
- **v2 (later):** ext-vendoring + repo-mode reading ext from the repo + djb's redaction policy.
→ **Recommend:** ship v1 now, v2 as a follow-on. This drops rop's "must ship together" risk and gets vox a working result sooner. Confirm the split.

**3. Write polarity (minor).** `ethos vendor` writes into git-tracked space. Make it **plan/`--dry-run`-by-default** (like `ethos team migrate`), execute on `--apply`, for both CLI and MCP.
→ **Recommend:** plan-by-default. Confirm or say write-by-default.

**Resolved as leader (folding into the ADR, no decision needed):** config key `resolution: layered|repo-only`; route *all* writes to repo in repo-only mode (rsc's write-then-invisible footgun); hard startup error when `repo-only` is set but no repo layer exists; enumerate the 5 read surfaces to gate; a single named owning package for the shared completeness-check (so vendor + doctor + the stores don't diverge — rsc's cross-mission risk); cut vendor flags 9→7 (drop `--no-teams`/`--from` that let you produce an incomplete "complete"); formatter lives in `internal/hook/format_output.go`; document the closure blast radius.

## Your `.local` idea is the clean answer

Split ext into two files per namespace:
- **`<handle>.ext/<ns>.yaml`** — shareable config. Vendored, committable. (quarry collections, voice, gpg key *id*.)
- **`<handle>.ext/<ns>.local.yaml`** — machine-specific or sensitive. Gitignored, **never vendored**. The escape hatch for the rare real secret.

Reads merge base + `.local` (local wins). This mirrors the org's existing convention — `.envrc`/`.envrc.local`, `vox.md`/`vox.local.md` — so it's a known pattern, not a new idea to learn.

**Why it beats default-off/redaction:** the boundary is *explicit in the layout* instead of a heuristic guessing which values look secret. Vendor's rule becomes trivial and safe: include `*.yaml`, always skip `*.local.yaml`. Ext defaults **on** (it's useful), and anything you don't want shared you put in `.local`. It dissolves the whole "commission djb to design redaction" problem — though a quick djb sanity-check on the convention is still cheap.

**Scope note:** this extends DES-008 (ext gains a base + `.local` merge on read). It's small and independently useful. My recommendation: **fold it into the ni0y design** as the ext-safety answer — it's the foundation that makes safe ext-vendoring possible, so it belongs in v1, not deferred.

Want me to send a design increment to bwk (who owns the ext read path) to spec the `.local` merge + gitignore + vendor-exclusion, and reconcile it into the ADR? Or do more discovery on the `.local` mechanics first?

## What I found (read before asserting)

Ext today: `&lt;handle&gt;.ext/&lt;namespace&gt;.yaml`, a flat YAML map, resolved **global-only** (`internal/identity/layered.go:54-55`, `ExtDir`→global at `layered.go:479-482`; DES-044). Three read paths unmarshal a namespace file: `loadExtensions` (`ext.go:221-249`, feeds `get_identity`/`whoami`/hooks via `store.go:85-86`), `ExtGet` (`ext.go:41-75`), and `extSetDirect`'s load-modify-write (`ext.go:110-128`). Constraints live in `ext.go:14-20, 262-280`. No repo-layer ext dirs exist yet — the `.punt-labs/ethos` here is the team submodule.

## Answers to the four required items

**Merge semantics.** One helper `readNamespace(handle, ns)` reads `&lt;ns&gt;.yaml`, then overlays `&lt;ns&gt;.local.yaml` per key (`local` wins), guarded by `os.IsNotExist`. `loadExtensions` and `ExtGet` route through it; `get_identity`/`whoami` return one flat merged namespace map — readers can't tell which key came from which file. No `.local` present = byte-identical to today. `ExtList` reports a namespace when either file exists, stripping the `.local` suffix so no phantom `quarry.local` namespace appears.

**Write targeting.** `ethos ext set --local` (MCP: `local bool`, default false). Default writes base; secrets need the explicit flag. Base writes must not fold `.local` keys into base (would leak the secret into the committable file). `ext get`/`ext list` return the merged/union view without revealing which keys are local. `ext del --local` deletes from the companion and warns if the key still resolves from the other file.

**Gitignore + vendor-exclusion invariant.** Repo rule `.punt-labs/ethos/**/*.local.yaml`, emitted by `ethos vendor` (and `ethos setup`) — global ext is already untracked. Vendor copies `&lt;ns&gt;.yaml`, **ALWAYS** skips `&lt;ns&gt;.local.yaml`; the file layout is the safety boundary, no heuristic redaction. This resolves the vendor design's open question §10.3 (`ni0y-vendor-command.md:377-379`).

**Back-compat.** No `.local` file ⇒ byte-identical output; the `.local` read is a pure addition.

## Record recommendation

New ADR (DES-0NN) amending DES-008 **by reference**, not an in-place edit — matches how DES-022 (`DESIGN.md:1362`) and DES-044 (`DESIGN.md:4038`) both extend the settled DES-008. Full Problem/Decision/Reasoning/Rejected-alternatives/Implications draft is in §8.

## Open questions / djb flags

1. Per-file vs union key cap (§3) — recommend per-file; minor.
2. **§7 flag:** `.local` does NOT change where ext resolves from. Today ext is global-only; the split is a per-directory merge that composes with whatever layer the resolution-mode ADR chooses. The global-vs-repo ext read is owned by `ni0y-resolution-mode.md`/`ni0y-vendor-command.md`, not this doc — both already flag the coupling.
3. **djb pass (§9):** one residual leak survives — a secret typed into base `&lt;ns&gt;.yaml` without `--local`. The partition is convention + default, not enforcement (DES-008 forbids ethos interpreting values). Recommend a warning-only, name-heuristic lint (`*_token`, `*_secret`, `password`, ...) at the vendor/commit boundary, with the curated pattern list owned by djb. Note: `gpg_key_id` is a public key ID, not a secret — so any name heuristic needs curation, which is exactly a djb call.</result>

[user] # /vox command

Enable or disable vox notifications, or switch TTS model/provider mid-session.

## Usage

- `/vox y` — enable vox (notifications on task completion and permission prompts)
- `/vox n` — disable vox (no notifications)
- `/vox c` — continuous mode (notifications on task completion, permission prompts, and real-time signals)
- `/vox model <name>` — switch TTS model (e.g. `v3`, `flash`, `turbo`)
- `/vox provider <name>` — switch TTS provider (e.g. `elevenlabs`, `openai`, `polly`, `say`)

## Implementation

Parse `y`:

### `y`

Call the `notify` MCP tool with `mode="y"`. No text output — the panel confirms.

### `n`

Call the `notify` MCP tool with `mode="n"`. No text output — the panel confirms.

### `c`

1. Call the `notify` MCP tool with `mode="c"`.
2. Call the `who` MCP tool to list voices.
3. Display featured voices with blurbs. Tell user they can pick with `/unmute @<name>`.

### `model <name>`

Resolve the model shorthand to full model ID:

- `v3` → `eleven_v3`
- `flash` → `eleven_flash_v2_5`
- `turbo` → `eleven_turbo_v2_5`
- `multilingual` → `eleven_multilingual_v2`
- Anything else → pass through as-is (e.g. `tts-1`, `tts-1-hd`)

Call the `unmute` MCP tool with only the `model` parameter (no text). Confirm: "Switched model to `<full_id>`."

### `provider <name>`

Call the `unmute` MCP tool with only the `provider` parameter (no text). When switching providers, also pass `model` as empty string to clear the previous provider's model from config. Confirm: "Switched provider to `<name>`."

Valid providers: `elevenlabs`, `openai`, `polly`, `say`, `espeak`.

### No argument or unrecognized

Tell user: "Usage: `/vox y|n|c`, `/vox model <name>`, `/vox provider <name>`"

## Verdict: APPROVE-WITH-CHANGES

The core architecture is sound: a single per-namespace base+`.local` merge, name-based total vendor skip, and gitignore as defense-in-depth. Citations are accurate on line numbers and the DES-008/022/044 SETTLED-status precedent for amendment-by-reference. Two design-level gaps and one path error should be resolved before implementation dispatches — all cheaper to fix in the design than to discover in a defect cycle.

### Findings (ranked)

**1. [HIGH] The DES-008 sidecar direct-read contract bypasses the merge — and the design does not address it.**
`DESIGN.md:167-168` explicitly permits tools to read `&lt;handle&gt;.ext/&lt;namespace&gt;.yaml` **directly** ("sidecar contract"). The design's central claim (§2, doc lines 71-73: "the one place a namespace file is read into a map, so every read surface inherits it") is true only for *ethos-mediated* reads. I confirmed every in-repo consumer routes through `ExtGet`/`loadExtensions`/`ExtList` (MCP `tools.go:357,388`; CLI `cmd/ethos/ext.go:77,112`; persona via `store.go:85`/`layered.go:55`) — so those inherit the merge. But an external tool exercising the DES-008 direct-read blessing sees **base only** and never sees `.local`.

Consequence: the safety property is intact regardless (a secret in `quarry.local.yaml` stays out of git and out of vendor no matter who reads). But the *functional* property is not: a machine-specific token placed in `.local` — the design's headline use case (§1) — never reaches a tool that reads its namespace file directly. The design should explicitly scope the overlay: "`.local` is visible only to ethos-mediated readers; a tool exercising the DES-008 sidecar direct-read contract gets base only." Then decide whether that is acceptable (memory wiring reaches agents via the ethos hook path per DES-022 `DESIGN.md:1821`, so it is — but a direct-reading tool needing a secret is not served). One paragraph in design; a silent no-op secret in implementation.

**2. [MEDIUM] `ExtDel` is a fourth namespace-unmarshal site, omitted from §2's "three read paths."**
`ext.go:170-180` reads and unmarshals a namespace file on single-key delete; §2 enumerates only `loadExtensions`, `ExtGet`, `extSetDirect`. `ExtDel` must NOT route through the merged `readNamespace` (delete targets one file), which is consistent with §3's del semantics — but because §2 undercounts it, the implementer may leave `ExtDel` `.local`-unaware. Then `ext del &lt;ns&gt; --local` and whole-namespace `ext del &lt;ns&gt;` (which removes only base, `ext.go:156-165`) would orphan the companion, and the "still resolves from `quarry.local.yaml`" warning (§3) would never fire. Name `ExtDel` in the enumeration and specify its `.local` targeting.

**3. [MEDIUM] `readNamespace` misuse is the real form of the base-fold-local risk.**
The base-must-not-fold-local hazard (§3) is real but narrow: today `extSetDirect` reads base-only (`ext.go:109-128`), so no leak exists in the current write path. The danger is an implementer's instinct to "route everything through `readNamespace`" — a load-modify-`writeBase` using the merged map would fold every `.local` key into the committable base. The mitigation (keep `extSetDirect` base-only) is correct and matches current code. Strengthen it into a **contract on the helper**: `readNamespace` doc-comment states "read-only merged view; never marshal its result back to a file." Cheap, and it prevents the one refactor that reintroduces the leak.

**4. [MEDIUM] Gitignore emission has a "before vendor/setup ever runs" hole.**
§4 assigns rule emission to `vendor` and `setup`. A hand-authored `.punt-labs/ethos/` — or a future repo-layer `.local` created by `ext set --local` — that predates either command has no ignore rule, so `git add -A` commits the secret. Today this is not reachable (ext writes global-only: `layered.go:492-497` → `global.extSetDirect`; §7 correctly defers repo-ext reads to the resolution-mode ADR), so it is future-coupled. Two cheap closes: (a) attach the ignore-rule guarantee to whatever first creates a repo-layer `.local` file, not only to vendor/setup; (b) add an `ethos doctor` check that the rule exists whenever a repo `.punt-labs/ethos/` is present. Note this requirement for the repo-ext-write ADR so it does not fall between the two.

**5. [LOW] `ExtList` suffix-strip order is a correctness trap.**
`.local.yaml` also satisfies `HasSuffix(".yaml")` — today's `strings.TrimSuffix(e.Name(), ".yaml")` (`ext.go:213`) already yields the phantom `quarry.local` the design wants to prevent. The fix must strip `.local.yaml` **as a unit and before** the `.yaml` case, else the union carries `quarry.local` instead of `quarry`. State the check order in §2 so the implementer does not TrimSuffix `.yaml` first.

**6. [LOW] Package-path citation error.**
The design says `internal/attribute/ext.go` throughout; the file is `internal/identity/ext.go` (there is no `attribute/ext.go`). Line numbers are all accurate and the proposed `func (s *Store) readNamespace` signature is correct for the `identity` package. Fix the path so the implementer is not misdirected.

### On bwk's open questions

**Per-file vs union key cap (§3): keep per-file.** The `MaxKeysPerNS` cap (`ext.go:18,131`) exists to bound file size; that intent is per-file. A union cap forces a cross-file read on every write for no size benefit and complicates the base-only write contract (finding 3). Check the cap on the targeted file, as the current code already does. Not a minor question — per-file is the correct answer, not merely the simpler one.

**Base-secret leak / heuristic lint (§9): ship the partition now; defer the lint, do not block on it.** The safety boundary already means a secret typed into base without `--local` leaks only if the operator *also* commits/vendors it — and the value is then visible in the diff, not hidden. That is an acceptable residual for this increment. A warning-only lint is reasonable defense-in-depth, but note the tension the design soft-pedals: inspecting **key names** against a secret-ish pattern list is itself a form of ethos interpreting ext content, which is exactly the DES-008 invariant (`DESIGN.md:170-171`) the whole partition was chosen to preserve. It is defensible only as **non-blocking advisory** and must be documented as a heuristic that ethos does not act on. It is a djb-owned follow-up, not a dependency of this ADR.

### Assessed clean

- **Merge routing** (loadExtensions + ExtGet → readNamespace): complete for all ethos-mediated readers; I confirmed no in-repo surface reads namespace files outside `ext.go`. `os.IsNotExist` guarding is correct.
- **Back-compat**: byte-identical with no `.local` holds across `loadExtensions`, `ExtGet`, `extSetDirect`, `ExtList`, and `ExtDel` — the base map/base file is returned unchanged in each.
- **Vendor skip**: name-based, total, no value inspection — airtight as the primary boundary and correctly independent of the gitignore rule.
- **Amendment-by-reference (§8)**: grounded. DES-008 (`DESIGN.md:106`), DES-022 (`1362`), DES-044 (`4038`) are all SETTLED, and 022/044 are the exact precedent of extending 008 with a cross-referencing record. Right call over an in-place edit.
- **Coupling (§7)**: the per-directory merge composes with both sibling designs (`docs/ni0y-vendor-command.md`, `docs/ni0y-resolution-mode.md`, both present) without contradiction; layer choice correctly deferred.

Relevant files: `/Users/jfreeman/Coding/punt-labs/ethos/docs/ni0y-ext-local.md`, `/Users/jfreeman/Coding/punt-labs/ethos/internal/identity/ext.go`, `/Users/jfreeman/Coding/punt-labs/ethos/internal/identity/layered.go`, `/Users/jfreeman/Coding/punt-labs/ethos/internal/identity/store.go`, `/Users/jfreeman/Coding/punt-labs/ethos/DESIGN.md` (lines 106, 167-171, 1362, 1821, 4038).</result>

</task-notification>

[assistant] rsc's `.local` review: **APPROVE-WITH-CHANGES** — architecture sound, 6 fixable design gaps. Notable ones I'll fold in:
- **[HIGH] scope the overlay:** `.local` is visible only to *ethos-mediated* reads; a tool exercising DES-008's direct-read blessing sees base only. Safety holds (secret stays out of git/vendor regardless), but `.local` isn't a general secret store for direct-reading tools — needs to be stated explicitly.
- Make `readNamespace` a read-only merged view (never marshal back → prevents folding `.local` into base); `ExtDel` is a 4th read path to handle; gitignore rule needs an owner for the "before vendor ever runs" case + a `doctor` check.
