# Security review: `.local` ext-secrets boundary (ethos-ni0y)

## Verdict: SOUND-WITH-CHANGES

The partition strategy is the right shape — a file-layout boundary beats value redaction, and it keeps the DES-008 no-interpretation invariant intact. Reading a *key name* is not interpreting a *value*, so the name-heuristic lint I recommend below is DES-008-clean. But the boundary rests on two load-bearing assumptions the design states in prose and does not enforce in mechanism: (a) filename declares content ("`.local.yaml` = secret"), and (b) a base write never folds `.local` keys. Both are bypassable. Three changes turn "sound convention" into "sound control."

---

## Q1 — Enumeration: every place ext content reaches git-tracked space

I traced `id.Ext` (populated only by `loadExtensions`, `store.go:85` / `layered.go:55`) to every sink:

| Sink | Git-tracked? | Embeds ext? | Leak? |
|------|-------------|-------------|-------|
| `ethos vendor` → `.punt-labs/ethos/identities/&lt;h&gt;.ext/&lt;ns&gt;.yaml` | **Yes** | Copies base file bytes | Only via the two bypasses below |
| Agent generation `.claude/agents/&lt;h&gt;.md` (`generate_agents.go:283` `buildAgentFile`) | **Yes** | **No** — uses personality/writing-style/role/talents only, never `id.Ext` | **None** (positive finding) |
| SessionStart / PreCompact `session_context` injection (`extension_context.go:11` `BuildExtensionContext`) | No (runtime context) | Yes — reads merged view incl. `.local` | Runtime/quarry exposure, not git (see Q5) |
| `ethos show` / `whoami` / `get_identity` MCP (`main.go:354`) | No (stdout) | Yes — merged view | Only if operator pipes to a tracked file (see Q5) |
| `ethos export` (soulspec/claude-md) | Yes (foreign files) | **No** — lossy, drops ext by contract (`export.go:20`) | **None** |
| Vendor manifest `.vendor.yaml` / `missions.jsonl` | Yes | Paths/handles only, no values | **None** |

**The only committed sink that carries ext content is `ethos vendor`.** Agent-file generation — my prime suspect, since `.claude/agents/` is committed (commit 8debdb0) — does not touch `id.Ext`. That closes the largest worry.

Two bypasses of the vendor name-filter remain:

- **F1 (HIGH) — symlink / non-regular-file bypass.** The filter is name-based: "skip `*.local.yaml`." It trusts that `&lt;ns&gt;.yaml` holds base content. If `quarry.yaml` is a symlink to `quarry.local.yaml` (or to `~/.ssh/id_rsa`, or `~/.env`), a byte-verbatim copy (`ni0y-vendor-command.md:161`) follows the link and writes the secret into a committed regular file. `extSetDirect`'s `os.WriteFile` (`ext.go:140`) also follows symlinks. Fix: vendor copies **regular files only** — `lstat` each ext entry, skip/refuse symlinks, devices, and anything non-regular; document that ext base files must be real files.

- **F2 (HIGH) — base write folds `.local`.** `extSetDirect` (`ext.go:110-128`) today reads `s.extPath` = the **base** file, mutates, rewrites base. Under this design the trap is trivial: if the load step is refactored to call the new merged `readNamespace`, a base write reads base+local, then writes the union back to base — silently promoting every `.local` secret into the committable file. The design names this rule (§3) but it is exactly the kind of "obviously correct" thing an implementer collapses into one helper. This must be a **tested invariant**, not a comment: assert that `ext set mal quarry k v` (no `--local`), with `k` pre-existing in `quarry.local.yaml`, leaves `quarry.yaml` free of `k`.

---

## Q2 — Residual leak (secret in BASE): block, don't warn

Warning-only is insufficient at the commit boundary. A warning fires *after* vendor has already written the file into the working tree; it is one `git add` away, and in a `--all`/CI invocation nobody reads stderr. "Fail closed, deny by default" applies: the command that puts bytes into git must refuse when those bytes are name-flagged as a credential.

**Recommended policy: two-tier name-heuristic, fail-closed at `ethos vendor`, advisory at `ethos doctor`.**

- **BLOCK tier** → vendor exits non-zero, names the `&lt;handle&gt; &lt;ns&gt;/&lt;key&gt;`, suggests `--local`. Override is **per-key only**: `--allow-ext-key &lt;ns&gt;/&lt;key&gt;` (repeatable, must name the exact key). No blanket `--force` — a reflexive bypass flag is a defeated control.
- **WARN tier** → stderr note, does not block.
- **Matching**: keys are already `^[a-z][a-z0-9_]*$` (grammar forces lowercase — no case-evasion). Match on **underscore-delimited token membership** plus whole-key equality, not raw substring (so `tokenizer` ≠ `token`). Values are **never** inspected — name-only keeps DES-008 intact.
- **Exclusions checked FIRST** (suppress both tiers) so public references don't trip it.

```
EXCLUDE (public references, never flag):
  any key ending _id          # gpg_key_id, key_id
  keyid  public_key  pubkey  fingerprint  keyserver  key_server  key_name

BLOCK (high-confidence secret material):
  password  passwd  passphrase  secret  token
  api_key  apikey  private_key  privkey  credential  credentials

WARN (review-worthy, ambiguous):
  key (bare or *_key not caught by EXCLUDE)  signing_key
  salt  seed  pin  otp  dsn  cookie
```

`gpg_key_id` → matches EXCLUDE (`_id`) first → clean. `memory_collection`, `session_context` → no token match → clean. `api_token` → token `token` → BLOCK. Curated so today's real ext keys and the one `gpg_key_id` all pass.

Run the identical lint in `ethos doctor` (advisory) so operators find the problem before they vendor.

---

## Q3 — Gitignore is not a sufficient control

No — a `.gitignore` rule is a single point of failure with four failure modes:

1. Edited or deleted — no signal.
2. `git add -f` bypasses it.
3. A repo that assembles `.punt-labs/ethos/` by hand and never runs `ethos vendor`/`ethos setup` never gets the rule.
4. **Gitignore does not untrack already-tracked files.** If a `.local.yaml` was committed before the rule existed, the rule is inert and the secret stays tracked.

Defense-in-depth (the name-based vendor skip is primary; gitignore only guards hand-authored `ext set --local`):

- **Vendor + doctor: `git ls-files` check** — error/warn if any `*.local.yaml` under `.punt-labs/ethos/` is already tracked. This is the catch for failure mode 4, and it is cheap.
- **doctor also asserts the gitignore rule is present** (failure modes 1, 3).
- **Optional git `pre-commit` hook** emitted by `ethos setup` that rejects staged `.punt-labs/ethos/**/*.local.yaml`. Note it's advisory (`--no-verify` defeats it) — it is a backstop, not the boundary.

The boundary holds without the gitignore *for vendored content* (vendor never copies `.local`). Gitignore + the tracked-file check together are adequate for hand-authored `.local` files. Gitignore alone is not.

---

## Q4 — ext-on-by-default: acceptable, conditioned on the block-lint

Yes — acceptable posture, given (a) the verified zero-secret state across 30 identities, (b) the name-based skip, and (c) the block-lint from Q2 shipping with it. Do **not** gate on interactive confirmation — a prompt is defeated in CI/scripts and trains operators to auto-confirm. The right fail-safe is *visibility + hard gate*, both cheap:

- Vendor already lists `ExtFiles` and (per `.local` design §5) prints `skipped N .local ext files`. Keep both — the operator sees the boundary held.
- The block-lint is the hard gate. Confirmation is theater; a non-suppressible-except-per-key block is control.

If the block-lint slips to a later increment, then flip to ext-**off**-by-default (`--with-ext` opt-in) until it lands. On-by-default without the lint is the only unacceptable combination.

---

## Q5 — Other trust-model issues

- **F5 (LOW) — `.local` protects git, not runtime.** The merged view (base+`.local`) flows into `session_context` injection, `ext get`, `whoami`, `get_identity`, and thus into the model context and PreCompact→quarry transcript capture. `.local` means "not committed," **not** "not exposed to the model or local tools." State this scope explicitly in the ADR so nobody assumes `.local` is a secrets vault. It is a git-exclusion mechanism, full stop. For real at-rest secrecy the values still shouldn't be genuine high-value credentials sitting in plaintext under `~/.punt-labs/`.

- **F6 (LOW) — merged-view serialization.** Any workflow that pipes `ext get`/`whoami`/`ethos show --json` into a tracked path commits the secret. Inherent to the merged view; one-line warning in the ADR ("never serialize the merged identity view into tracked space").

- **Note (informational) — global-base secrets.** Vendor reads base from the **global** layer today (`layered.go:479`). A secret typed into a *global* base `&lt;ns&gt;.yaml` (no `.local`) vendors and commits identically. The layer origin doesn't change the residual; the Q2 name-lint is the only catch. No extra mechanism needed, but the lint must run against whichever layer vendor sources from.

---

## `.local` convention — hardening required before implementation

Four items, in priority order:

1. **Vendor copies regular files only** (F1) — `lstat`, skip non-regular ext entries.
2. **Tested base-write-base-only invariant** (F2) — the load step of a base `ext set` must not route through the merged `readNamespace`.
3. **Block-lint + curated pattern list** (Q2) — fail-closed at vendor, advisory at doctor, per-key override only.
4. **doctor/vendor tracked-`.local` check + gitignore-present check** (Q3).

With these four, the layout boundary is a control, not just a convention. Without 1 and 2, it is bypassable by a symlink or a one-line refactor. The design (`docs/ni0y-ext-local.md`) is correct in strategy and should proceed; these are the enforcement gaps that must close in implementation, not new design questions.

Relevant files: `/Users/jfreeman/Coding/punt-labs/ethos/docs/ni0y-ext-local.md`, `/Users/jfreeman/Coding/punt-labs/ethos/docs/ni0y-vendor-command.md`, `/Users/jfreeman/Coding/punt-labs/ethos/internal/identity/ext.go` (`extSetDirect` at lines 92-141 is the F2 invariant site), `/Users/jfreeman/Coding/punt-labs/ethos/internal/hook/generate_agents.go` (`buildAgentFile` — confirmed does not embed ext), `/Users/jfreeman/Coding/punt-labs/ethos/internal/hook/extension_context.go` (`BuildExtensionContext` — merged-view runtime sink), `/Users/jfreeman/Coding/punt-labs/ethos/DESIGN.md:106-284` (DES-008).</result>
<usage><subagent_tokens>64929</subagent_tokens><tool_uses>11</tool_uses><duration_ms>226904</duration_ms></usage>
</task-notification>

[assistant] All reviews are in. **Every verdict is positive** — rsc APPROVE-WITH-CHANGES (resolution + ext-`.local`), rop APPROVE-WITH-CHANGES (vendor), djb **SOUND-WITH-CHANGES** (security). The design is solid; findings are enforcement details, not redesigns.

**djb's security pass — the important results:**
- **Good news, contained blast radius:** djb traced every path ext content could reach git. The *only* committed sink is `ethos vendor`. Agent-file generation (which writes to committed `.claude/agents/`) **does not embed ext** — confirmed. `export` drops it. So there's one door to guard, not many.
- **Two bypasses to close in implementation** (both HIGH, mechanical): vendor must copy **regular files only** (a symlink `quarry.yaml → quarry.local.yaml` or `→ ~/.ssh/id_rsa` would defeat the name-skip); and the base-write-stays-base-only rule must be a **tested invariant**, not a comment (else a refactor folds `.local` secrets into the committable file).
- **Scope clarity:** `.local` is a **git-exclusion** mechanism, not a secrets vault — the merged view still flows to the model/quarry at runtime. That goes in the ADR so nobody over-trusts it.

**One real decision for you — the lint posture (specialists split):**
- **djb: fail-closed** — `ethos vendor` **blocks** if a base ext key name looks like a credential (`api_key`, `token`, `password`…), with a curated EXCLUDE list so public refs like `gpg_key_id` pass, and a **per-key** override (`--allow-ext-key ns/key`, no blanket `--force`). Same check advisory in `doctor`. His argument: a warning fires *after* the file's written and is one `git add` away; CI ignores stderr. And reading a key *name* isn't interpreting a *value*, so it stays DES-008-clean.
- **rsc: warn-only** — cautious that any heuristic edges toward ethos interpreting ext.
- **Crucial coupling:** djb says ext-on-by-default is only acceptable **if the block-lint ships with it**; otherwise ext defaults off. So this choice also decides whether v1 can have ext-on (which vox wants).

→ **My recommendation: djb's fail-closed block-lint**, shipping with ext-on in v1. It's the only posture that keeps ext-on (vox's need) safe, the per-key override prevents it becoming a nuisance, and the name-only matching answers rsc's DES-008 concern.

**Confirming my two earlier recommendations (say if you object):** v1 = vendor core + repo-authoritative mode + ext-`.local` + djb's four hardening items, shipped together; `ethos vendor` is **plan/`--dry-run`-by-default**.

On your ruling on the lint, I'll write the **single reconciled DES-0NN ADR** (folding all four reviews' fixes), send it to vox for the consumer sanity-check, and bring it back for your final ratification before any code.

vox found a real hole, and they're right. This is exactly why the consumer sanity-check exists.

**The gap:** DES-057 *copies* ext into the repo (vendor) and *validates* it's present (completeness predicate) — but Part A preserved DES-044's "ext resolves from global," so repo-only mode never *reads* ext from the repo. On a global-less checkout: ext → global → absent → agents lose their quarry memory wiring. Criterion (a) fails, and the predicate (validates present) disagrees with the read-path (reads global). All three drafts flagged the coupling as an open question; my reconciliation didn't close it. That's on me.

Acknowledging vox and dispatching the fix — this needs a DES-044 carve-out, which I won't hand-wave since DES-044 is a settled invariant.

[assistant] Carve-out design is in flight (bwk/rsc, **m-2026-07-11-010**).

**Jim — status + why this matters:** vox's consumer sanity-check on PR #345 caught a real gap I own. DES-057 *copies* ext into the repo and *validates* it's present, but I preserved DES-044 (ext reads from global), so repo-only mode never actually *reads* the vendored ext. On a global-less checkout, the 15 agents would silently lose their quarry memory wiring — criterion (a) fails, and the completeness predicate contradicts the read-path. All three drafts flagged this coupling as an open question; my reconciliation didn't close it.

The fix is a **carve-out to the settled DES-044 invariant** (ext-through-global): in repo-only mode, read ext from the repo layer via the same `readNamespace` merge, and treat absent repo ext for a resolved identity as a miss (fail loud). Because it modifies a settled invariant, I put bwk/rsc on designing it precisely rather than hand-waving — the crux is the *miss rule* (ext is additive today, so "any missing ext = fail" would spuriously break identities that legitimately have none).

**I'm holding v1 dispatch** until the carve-out lands, rsc validates it, I fold it into DES-057, and vox re-confirms (a). This is the design-review gate working exactly as intended — cheaper to catch now than mid-implementation. I'll bring you the amended ADR.

<summary>Agent "Design ext-read repo-only carve-out" finished</summary>
<note>A task-notification fires each time this agent stops with no live background children of its own. The user can send it another message and resume it, so the same task-id may notify more than once.</note>
<result>Design written to `/Users/jfreeman/Coding/punt-labs/ethos/docs/ni0y-ext-read-carveout.md`. No code, no commit — for the leader to fold into DES-057.

## The gap, confirmed against code

In `resolution: repo-only`, identities/attributes read from the repo but ext still reads from global — every ext method on `LayeredStore` hardcodes `ls.global` (`internal/identity/layered.go:55,480-482,485-486,506`). A global-less checkout reads ext from an absent global dir, gets nothing, and every agent loses its quarry memory wiring. Meanwhile vendor's completeness predicate validates the *repo* ext file present (`docs/ni0y-vendor-command.md:358`). Predicate and read-path point at different directories — that is the DES-057 self-inconsistency.

## Gated surfaces

One `extStore(handle)` selector gated on `repoAuthoritative` (the Part A field), replacing every hardcoded `ls.global` in the ext methods, plus two write-adjacent sites (`Save` ext-mkdir `:263`, `relocateRepoVoice` `:133,138`). The identity-internal `loadExtensions`/`readNamespace` path is store-relative (`ext.go:221-249`, `ext.go:28-38`), so the switch is a choice of `*Store`, not a rewrite — `ls.repo.loadExtensions` gives the repo dir merged base+`.local` for free.

## The miss rule (the crux)

Neither "any absent ext = miss" (fails every minimal identity spuriously) nor "consumer-declared required" (DES-008 forbids ethos interpreting ext). Recommended third rule: **the required-ext set is the `.vendor.yaml` manifest** — ethos's own artifact. A miss is a manifest-recorded ext base file absent from the source-layer `&lt;h&gt;.ext/`, folded into `ErrIncompleteRepoSet`. vox holds (vendor records `quarry.yaml`; absence is loud); minimal/hand-authored identities never fail (no manifest entry = no requirement). Surfaces via Part A's existing table: doctor FAIL, agent-generation fail, session-start degrade.

## DES-044 carve-out wording

Amend-by-reference: DES-044 holds unchanged in `layered` mode (ext through global, byte-identical); in `repo-only` mode ext resolves through the repo — the identity's source layer, global dropped, Part C base+`.local` merge — and writes target the repo. The no-interpretation invariant is untouched: layer selection is a directory choice, and the required-set is read from the manifest, never from a consumer value.

## Three open questions flagged for you

1. Manifest as the required-ext set (recommended — only record on a global-less checkout) vs the weaker directory-exists rule that can't distinguish "vendor forgot quarry.yaml" from "no ext."
2. Live `Load` additive-with-verdict (recommended, matches Part A degrade/gate split) vs live `Load` hard-fail.
3. Bundle-sourced ext writes: error like `Update` (recommended) vs allow a repo override.

Evaluator on this mission is `rsc`, not `djb` — flagging since the write-set is design-only.</result>
<usage><subagent_tokens>89028</subagent_tokens><tool_uses>10</tool_uses><duration_ms>299012</duration_ms></usage>
</task-notification>

**The miss rule — the hard part — is solved elegantly:** the required-ext set is **the `.vendor.yaml` manifest** (ethos's own artifact). A miss = a manifest-recorded ext file absent from the source layer. vox holds (vendor records `quarry.yaml` → absence is loud); minimal/hand-authored identities never fail spuriously (no manifest entry = no requirement). And it keeps DES-008 intact — the required-set comes from ethos's manifest, never from interpreting a consumer value.

[assistant] **The problem.** Ethos resolves an identity's data (personality, memory wiring, roles, team) from the repo-local `.punt-labs/ethos/` first, then falls back to the global registry on your machine. That fallback silently masks incompleteness: a repo that vendored a partial set still resolves the missing pieces from global, so it *looks* portable but isn't — clone it somewhere without your global home and identities quietly vanish. DES-057 makes a repo genuinely self-standing.

**The design — three coupled parts.** (1) **`ethos vendor`** walks the full dependency graph of an identity — including the reverse "which teams contain this person" edge that pulls in otherwise-missed members — and snapshots a complete, resolvable set into the repo, recording exactly what it wrote in a `.vendor.yaml` manifest. (2) **Repo-authoritative mode** (`resolution: repo-only`, opt-in) turns off the global fallback so the repo is the sole source; if anything the manifest says should be there is missing, it fails loud and names it, instead of silently degrading. (3) **ext `.local` split** — extension config (like each agent's quarry memory wiring) is now vendored by default because it's useful and secret-free, while a `<ns>.local.yaml` companion holds anything machine-specific or sensitive and is *never* vendored; that file-layout boundary keeps secrets out of git without ethos ever inspecting a value.

**Why it's safe and correct.** Everything is opt-in — unset config and absent `.local` behave byte-identically to today. The secret boundary is structural (skip `*.local.yaml`, copy regular files only, fail-closed if a base key *name* looks like a credential) rather than a fragile content scrubber, which keeps the "ethos never interprets ext values" invariant intact. And the produce side and the read side share one predicate — vendor validates exactly what repo-only mode reads (the manifest) — so they can't drift. The consumer (vox) caught the one real gap during review (vendored ext wasn't actually being *read* in repo-only mode), which a DES-044 carve-out closed; vox has since signed off that all three acceptance criteria pass.
